Benchmarks

Benchmark Evidence, Not a Leaderboard

The website renders committed static artifacts. Benchmark timing is interpreted beside the generated current-support matrix instead of restating support posture here.

Optimization triage

Start with the largest measured ShardLoom-owned route costs.

This board is generated from the route-share artifact table. It ranks route work by dominant measured stage cost, then keeps claim state and artifact freshness beside the timing so optimization direction does not become a public performance claim.

Current support source

Benchmarks reuse the status matrix.

Runtime support counts come from docs/status/runs-today-support-matrix.json. The benchmark artifact supplies timing and coverage context; it is not the source of truth for support claims.

33support rows
18executable
5feature-gated
5claim/platform blocked

Support claim boundary: current-state discoverability only; this matrix does not expand runtime support or authorize production, package, performance, object-store, lakehouse, Foundry, REST, or Spark-replacement claims.

Public front doors

Route rows name the user-facing prepared paths.

The benchmark bundle publishes route-identity rows for the high-level Python front doors. These rows are not timing rows; they bind the public surface to the route lane, preparation boundary, reuse manifest, and no-fallback posture. For one-off SQL, Python, DataFrame, or CLI requests, the side-effect-free shardloom route facade reports the same route-admission boundary before any data read, query execution, sink write, or timing claim.

Front door not_timing_row_route_identity_only

ShardLoom Prepare-Once First Query

ctx.prepare_vortex('fact.csv', dim='dim.csv', workspace='target/shardloom-prepared').query('selective filter').collect()

Route timing dashboard

Route lanes are the comparison surface.

Stage pieces explain a ShardLoom route; they are not competing product lanes. Warm prepared and native Vortex rows stay labeled by start state.

Stage attribution

ShardLoom stage pieces explain route cost.

Preparation, query, output, evidence, and diagnostic context are separated from route-level comparisons so a warm prepared slice cannot be read as a cold end-to-end route. The benchmark artifact now keeps source admission, source-read scout timing, projection-aware text decode masks, row materialization status, lazy source-state family timing, Vortex array/write timing, prepared-state lookup timing, and result-sink evidence visible as code-backed attribution rather than route-total substitutes.

ShardLoom Prepare-Once Batch120n/an/a0.42 ms0.00 ms3.38 msn/a5.37 ms0.29 ms0.29 ms4.57 ms7.84 ms22.91 ms
ShardLoom Cold Certified Route1200.01 ms9.25 ms50.58 msn/a120.72 ms3.17 msn/a3.68 msn/a2.88 ms0.14 ms196.41 ms
ShardLoom Warm Prepared Query120n/an/an/an/an/an/an/a0.32 ms0.32 ms4.86 ms7.54 ms16.95 ms
ShardLoom Native Vortex Query120n/an/an/an/an/an/an/a0.33 ms0.33 ms4.87 ms7.40 ms16.86 ms

Schema: shardloom.website.route_runtime_status.v1. Boundary: stage attribution explains why a ShardLoom route took time; stage pieces are not competing product lanes.

Inclusion schema: shardloom.route_timing_stage_inclusion.v1. Boundary: stage inclusion metadata makes route totals auditable; it does not convert diagnostic stage fields into comparable route totals or authorize speed claims.

Digest policy schema: shardloom.traditional_analytics.source_admission_digest_policy.v1. Boundary: metadata-first source admission is local benchmark reuse evidence only; publication/claim-grade rows must request full digest verification when required.

Lazy family schema: shardloom.website.source_state_lazy_family.v1. Boundary: source-state family construction evidence is runtime work-avoidance attribution only; it is not a performance or superiority claim until benchmark rerun and claim gates pass.

Route-share attribution

Optimization targets follow route share.

Route totals remain the comparison surface. The Amdahl table identifies the largest measured stage per ShardLoom route, while source-read scout, projection-aware decode, Vortex writer-context, and Vortex reopen/scan tables show which split evidence is complete or still blocked before stronger optimization claims.

Route-shape guard

Route lanes and source-array boundaries are explicit.

HOTPATH-1/HOTPATH-5 add route-shape stratification fields and a source-to-Vortex-array guard so cold, prepared, native, and external-baseline rows cannot be compared without their start state, end state, route lane, and inclusive-versus-exclusive import boundary. Current route timing values come from the latest promoted artifact only.

RouteScenarioLaneFamilyStartEndRow classStage scopeNo fallback
Awaiting refreshed benchmark artifact after the current optimization batch.
RouteScenarioStatusProviderInput layoutRecord batchesExclusive fieldInclusive parentNo fallback
Awaiting refreshed benchmark artifact after the current optimization batch.

Route-shape rows in current artifact: 0. Source-array guard rows in current artifact: 0. Rust and the benchmark harness emit the `route_shape_*` and `source_to_vortex_array_guard_*` fields; timing interpretation stays tied to the latest promoted artifact.

Runtime fast path

Runtime timing is separate from output and evidence rendering.

Sub-ms prepared/native query work can coexist with larger sink or evidence-render costs because route timing, output delivery, evidence capture, and certificate linkage are reported as separate buckets.

Artifact table: Runtime Fast Path Versus Evidence Path.

Schema: shardloom.route_fast_path_attribution.v1. Boundary: runtime execution timing, output delivery, evidence capture, evidence render, and certificate linking are separate interpretation buckets; fast-path timing is not a performance superiority claim.

Evidence and sink tiers

Hot lanes can stay compact without weakening publication proof.

Prepared/native benchmark rows report the requested evidence tier, actual tier, sink tier, route-total sink inclusion, and skip reasons. Compact local rows can avoid human rendering and replay work only when the row is non-publication/non-claim-grade.

Evidence-render proof

Human benchmark evidence is regenerated from compact facts.

Evidence-render proof fields carry compact route facts, digest evidence, no-fallback markers, and a claim boundary so the promoter and website can expand human tables outside the hot Rust route. Current route timing values come from the latest promoted artifact.

Result-sink capillary

Native result output is separated from compatibility fanout.

Requested result sinks carry scalar JSON byte/digest evidence, native Vortex output selection, compatibility fanout selection, replay digest parity, and explicit no-fallback fields. Current timing values remain artifact-bound evidence, not performance or replacement claims.

RouteScenarioStatusCapillary routeJSON bytesNative VortexCompat fanoutDigestNo fallback
Awaiting refreshed benchmark artifact after the current optimization batch.

Capillary rows in current artifact: 0. Rust emits the `result_sink_capillary_*` fields; public route timing values remain tied to the latest promoted artifact.

Operator mode inventory

Runtime support is not encoded-native support.

Rows can be scoped-runtime-supported while their operators remain residual-native or materialized-temporary. Encoded-native execution is a separate claim with its own blocker code and promotion candidate.

Prepare-once reuse

Amortization is shown as route math.

The prepared route keeps first-query cost visible, then shows how the same preparation cost amortizes across repeated prepared executions. Refreshed artifacts can also expose prepared-state manifest lookup, cache hit, miss-create, artifact write, register, replay verification, and attractor-key evidence.

Benchmark constitution

Rows need route, correctness, environment, and no-fallback proof before claims.

The manifest names the row validator and the field set required before any benchmark row can become claim-grade. Current static artifacts remain interpretation evidence, not public performance claims.

Cold-lane attribution

Cold ingest bottlenecks stay attached to the route.

The promoter classifies each row before publication and labels the dominant cold-stage bottleneck. Missing stage splits block claim-grade interpretation instead of letting cold preparation or harness overhead hide inside a single timing number. The page should be refreshed with the post-optimization artifact whenever source-normalization or writer-stage performance changes land; correctness-only sink-fidelity changes are reflected in status and use-case pages until a new timing artifact is promoted.

Runtime status

Runtime support is separate from claim readiness.

A row can be scoped-runtime-supported without authorizing performance, production, or Spark-replacement claims. External unsupported rows are baseline limitations, not ShardLoom runtime gaps.

ScopeRowsInterpretation
ShardLoom unsupported rows0ShardLoom runtime gaps in the promoted comparative roster
External baseline unsupported rows6External engine limitation rows; not ShardLoom runtime gaps
route_runtime_status=external_baseline_only720published row status vocabulary
route_runtime_status=scoped_runtime_supported600published row status vocabulary

Status vocabulary: external_baseline_only, feature_gated, fixture_smoke_only, scoped_runtime_supported, unsupported.

Claim-gate distribution

Evidence quality is not the same as runtime support.

Timing rows remain local context, not superiority proof. Compatibility cold timing is not pure query speed. Runtime support, evidence quality, and claim authorization are shown as separate layers.
